# big-code-flink-arch-001: Flink Checkpoint Coordination Architecture

## Task

Map the Flink checkpoint coordination architecture: how the JobManager triggers a checkpoint, propagates barriers through the task graph, and coordinates acknowledgments. Trace the complete distributed two-phase commit from CheckpointCoordinator through barrier injection, barrier alignment/processing at downstream tasks, state snapshot, acknowledgment, to CompletedCheckpoint.

## Context

- **Repository**: apache/flink (Java, ~3.5M LOC)
- **Category**: Architectural Understanding
- **Difficulty**: hard
- **Subsystem Focus**: flink-runtime/checkpoint/ and flink-streaming-java/runtime/io/checkpointing/

## Requirements

1. Identify all relevant components in the checkpoint coordination flow (JobManager-side coordinator, RPC dispatch, barrier events, barrier handlers, state snapshot, acknowledgment)
2. Trace the dependency chain from CheckpointCoordinator.triggerCheckpoint() through barrier propagation to CompletedCheckpoint
3. Document the aligned vs unaligned checkpoint barrier handling (SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler vs CheckpointBarrierTracker)
4. Explain the PendingCheckpoint lifecycle and the ack-based completion protocol

## Expected Output

Write your analysis to `/logs/agent/solution.md` with the following structure:

```
## Files Examined
- path/to/file1.ext — role in architecture
- path/to/file2.ext — role in architecture
...

## Dependency Chain
1. Entry point: path/to/entry.ext
2. Calls: path/to/next.ext (via function/method name)
3. Delegates to: path/to/impl.ext
...

## Analysis
[Detailed architectural analysis including:
- Design patterns identified
- Component responsibilities
- Data flow description
- Interface contracts between components]

## Summary
[Concise 2-3 sentence summary answering the task question]
```

## Evaluation Criteria

- File recall: Did you find the correct set of architecturally relevant files?
- Dependency accuracy: Did you trace the correct dependency/call chain?
- Architectural coherence: Did you correctly identify the design patterns and component relationships?

## What Was Written

The document covers 13 sections with full code-level detail:

### Section 1 — Coordinator Trigger
- `triggerCheckpoint(isPeriodic)` → `triggerCheckpointFromCheckpointThread` → timer thread serialization
- `CheckpointRequestDecider` admission control: `maxConcurrentCheckpoints`, `minPauseBetweenCheckpoints`, savepoint priority bypass
- `startTriggeringCheckpoint` async pipeline across `executor` (I/O) and `timer` (coordinator lock) threads
- `createPendingCheckpoint`: builds `notYetAcknowledgedTasks` map, registers `CheckpointCanceller` timeout, inserts into `pendingCheckpoints`
- Coordinator and master state snapshots run **before** tasks are triggered (required for `ExternallyInducedSource`)
- `triggerTasks`: builds `CheckpointOptions` (alignment type), iterates `getTasksToTrigger()` (source tasks only)

### Section 2–3 — Task Trigger and Snapshot
- RPC chain: `Execution` → `RpcTaskManagerGateway` → `TaskExecutor` → `Task` → `StreamTask`
- Unaligned checkpoints use `MailOptions.urgent()` to front-queue the mailbox action
- `SubtaskCheckpointCoordinatorImpl.checkpointState()` five steps: pre-abort check → `prepareSnapshotPreBarrier` → `broadcastEvent(CheckpointBarrier)` → alignment timer → `channelStateWriter.finishOutput` → `takeSnapshotSync` + `finishAndReportAsync`
- `AsyncCheckpointRunnable` materializes operator state futures on a thread pool, then calls `RpcCheckpointResponder.acknowledgeCheckpoint()` back to the JobManager

### Key architectural findings documented:

1. **Single-thread serialization**: All coordinator decisions run on a dedicated timer thread under a single `lock` object; acknowledgment processing and trigger decisions are fully serialized.

2. **Async pipeline**: `startTriggeringCheckpoint` is a `CompletableFuture` chain alternating between `executor` (I/O) and `timer` (lock-holding) threads — plan calculation and storage initialization are off the coordinator lock.

3. **Barrier priority mechanism**: Unaligned barriers are written as priority events in network subpartitions, causing them to physically overtake buffered data. `CheckpointedInputGate` processes these via `MailOptions.urgent()` mailbox mails.

4. **6-state Barr

Step 3: `registerAlignmentTimer()` \u2014 for timeoutable checkpoints\n   - Step 4: `channelStateWriter.finishOutput(checkpointId)` \u2014 if channel state needed\n   - Step 5: `takeSnapshotSync()` \u2192 `operatorChain.snapshotState()` \u2192 `finishAndReportAsync()`\n\n5. **Barrier Reception \u2014 CheckpointedInputGate**:\n   - `pollNext()` \u2192 `handleEvent()` \u2192 dispatches to `barrierHandler.processBarrier()` or `processBarrierAnnouncement()` or `processCancellationBarrier()`\n   - For unaligned: `EventAnnouncement` arrives first (priority event), triggers `processBarrierAnnouncement()`\n   - Priority events processed via `waitForPriorityEvents()` \u2192 mailbox urgent\n\n6. **BarrierHandlerState state machine** (for exactly-once, SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler):\n   - States: `WaitingForFirstBarrier`, `CollectingBarriers`, `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier`, `AlternatingCollectingBarriers`, `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned`, `AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned`\n   - Aligned path: `WaitingForFirstBarrier` \u2192 (first barrier) \u2192 `CollectingBarriers` \u2192 (all barriers) \u2192 trigger \u2192 `WaitingForFirstBarrier`\n   - Alternating (timeoutable) path: `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier` \u2192 (first barrier) \u2192 `AlternatingCollectingBarriers` \u2192 (timeout) \u2192 `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned` \u2192 (barrier) \u2192 `AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned` \u2192 (all barriers) \u2192 trigger \u2192 `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier`\n   - Pure unaligned: `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned` \u2192 (first barrier) \u2192 triggers immediately \u2192 `AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned`\n\n7. **CheckpointBarrierTracker** (at-least-once):\n   - No channel blocking\n   - Maintains `ArrayDeque<CheckpointBarrierCount>` of pending checkpoints (max 50)\n   - On barrier: find or create `CheckpointBarrierCount`, increment counter\n   - When `alignedChannels.size() == targetChannelCount`: trigger checkpoint\n   - Supports `CancelCheckpointMarker` for abort propagation\n   - Fast path for single-channel: trigger immediately\n\n8. **PendingCheckpoint lifecycle**:\n   - Created with `notYetAcknowledgedTasks` map (all tasks to wait for)\n   - `acknowledgeTask()`: removes from `notYetAcknowledgedTasks`, adds to `acknowledgedTasks`, updates `operatorStates`, records stats\n   - `isFullyAcknowledged()`: tasks + coordinators + master states all acknowledged\n   - `finalizeCheckpoint()`: writes `CheckpointMetadata` to `CheckpointMetadataOutputStream`, creates `CompletedCheckpoint`\n   - `abort()`: completes `onCompletionPromise` exceptionally, calls `dispose(releaseState=true)`\n\n9. **CompletedCheckpoint**:\n   - Immutable record: checkpointID, timestamps, operatorStates map, masterHookStates, storageLocation, externalPointer\n   - Stored in `CompletedCheckpointStore` (ZooKeeper or filesystem HA)\n\n10. **Acknowledgment flow**:\n    - `AsyncCheckpointRunnable.run()` \u2192 `finalizeNonFinishedSnapshots()` \u2192 `reportCompletedSnapshotStates()` \u2192 `taskEnvironment.getTaskStateManager().reportTaskStateSnapshots()` \u2192 `checkpointResponder.acknowledgeCheckpoint()` (RpcCheckpointResponder) \u2192 `checkpointCoordinatorGateway.acknowledgeCheckpoint()` (RPC to JobManager)\n    - `CheckpointCoordinator.receiveAcknowledgeMessage()` \u2192 `pendingCheckpoint.acknowledgeTask()` \u2192 if `isFullyAcknowledged()` \u2192 `completePendingCheckpoint()`\n\n11. **completePendingCheckpoint()**:\n    - `completedCheckpointStore.getSharedStateRegistry().checkpointCompleted(checkpointId)`\n    - `finalizeCheckpoint(pendingCheckpoint)` \u2192 `pendingCheckpoint.finalizeCheckpoint()` \u2192 writes metadata, returns `CompletedCheckpoint`\n    - The protocol is driven by a single `CheckpointCoordinator` on the JobManager and\npropagated through the operator graph via in-band `CheckpointBarrier` events. This document traces\nthe complete flow from coordinator trigger through barrier propagation to `CompletedCheckpoint`,\ncovering both aligned and unaligned barrier handling and the full `PendingCheckpoint` lifecycle.\n\n---\n\n## 1. Coordinator Trigger \u2014 JobManager Side\n\n### 1.1 Entry Points\n\n```\nCheckpointCoordinator.triggerCheckpoint(isPeriodic)\n  \u2514\u2500 triggerCheckpointFromCheckpointThread(checkpointProperties, null, isPeriodic)\n       \u2514\u2500 timer.execute(() -> triggerCheckpoint(props, location, isPeriodic))\n```\n\nAll checkpoint initiation \u2014 periodic, manual, and savepoint \u2014 funnels through\n`triggerCheckpointFromCheckpointThread`, which posts the actual trigger onto the coordinator's\ndedicated timer thread. This serializes all checkpoint decisions onto a single thread, avoiding\nlock contention with acknowledgment processing.\n\n### 1.2 Request Admission \u2014 CheckpointRequestDecider\n\nBefore any work begins, `chooseRequestToExecute(request)` consults `CheckpointRequestDecider`,\nwhich enforces:\n\n- **`maxConcurrentCheckpoints`** \u2014 rejects new periodic requests if `isTriggering` is true.\n- **`minPauseBetweenCheckpoints`** \u2014 compares `clock.relativeTimeMillis()` against\n  `lastCheckpointCompletionRelativeTime`; queues or drops the request if the pause has not elapsed.\n- **Savepoint priority** \u2014 savepoints bypass the concurrent-checkpoint limit and are never dropped.\n\nOnly if the decider returns a request does `startTriggeringCheckpoint` proceed.\n\n### 1.3 startTriggeringCheckpoint \u2014 Async Pipeline\n\n`startTriggeringCheckpoint` constructs a `CompletableFuture` chain that executes across two thread\npools: the coordinator's `executor` (I/O-capable) and the `timer` thread (single-threaded,\ncoordinator-wide lock holder).\n\n```\ncheckpointPlanCalculator.calculateCheckpointPlan()          [executor]\n  \u2514\u2500 checkpointIdCounter.getAndIncrement()                  [executor]\n       \u2514\u2500 createPendingCheckpoint(...) This ordering is\nrequired for `ExternallyInducedSource`: the coordinator must checkpoint before tasks so that\nsource-driven checkpoint IDs are consistent.\n\n### 1.4 triggerTasks \u2014 Dispatching to TaskManagers\n\n```java\n// CheckpointCoordinator.triggerTasks()\nCheckpointOptions checkpointOptions = CheckpointOptions.forConfig(\n    type,\n    checkpoint.getCheckpointStorageLocation().getLocationReference(),\n    isExactlyOnceMode,\n    unalignedCheckpointsEnabled,\n    alignedCheckpointTimeout);\n\nfor (Execution execution : checkpoint.getCheckpointPlan().getTasksToTrigger()) {\n    acks.add(execution.triggerCheckpoint(checkpointId, timestamp, checkpointOptions));\n}\n```\n\nOnly **source tasks** (tasks with no upstream inputs) are in `getTasksToTrigger()`. The RPC returns an\n`Acknowledge` future; `triggerTasks` collects all futures and waits via `FutureUtils.waitForAll`.\n\n---\n\n## 2. Task-Level Trigger \u2014 TaskManager Side\n\n### 2.1 Task \u2192 StreamTask\n\n```\nTask.triggerCheckpointBarrier(checkpointId, timestamp, checkpointOptions)\n  \u2514\u2500 ((CheckpointableTask) invokable).triggerCheckpointAsync(checkpointMetaData, checkpointOptions)\n```\n\n`Task` validates that the invokable implements `CheckpointableTask` and that the task is still\nrunning before delegating.\n\n### 2.2 StreamTask Mailbox Dispatch\n\n```java\n// StreamTask.triggerCheckpointAsync()\nif (checkpointOptions.isUnalignedCheckpoint()) {\n    mailboxExecutor.execute(MailboxExecutor.MailOptions.urgent(), this::triggerCheckpointAsyncInMailbox, ...);\n} else {\n    mailboxExecutor.execute(this::triggerCheckpointAsyncInMailbox, ...);\n}\n```\n\nUnaligned checkpoints use `MailOptions.urgent()`, which inserts the mail at the front of the\nmailbox queue. This ensures the barrier is emitted before any buffered records are processed,\npreserving the \"barrier overtakes data\" semantics of unaligned checkpoints.\n\n### 2.3 triggerCheckpointAsyncInMailbox\n\n```\ntriggerCheckpointAsyncInMailbox()\n  \u2514\u2500 subtaskCheckpointCoordinator.initInputsCheckpoint(checkpointId, options)\n  \u2514\u2500 performCheckpoint(checkpointMetaData, checkpointOptions, checkpointMetrics)\n       \u2514\u2500 subtaskCheckpointCoordinator.checkpointState(metadata, options, metrics, operatorChain, ...)\n```\n\n`initInputsCheckpoint` is called first for unaligned and timeoutable checkpoints to start the\n`ChannelStateWriter` before the barrier is broadcast, ensuring in-flight input buffers are captured\nfrom the moment the checkpoint begins.\n\n---\n\n## 3. Barrier Broadcast and State Snapshot \u2014 SubtaskCheckpointCoordinatorImpl\n\n`checkpointState()` is the central method executing all snapshot work atomically from the\nperspective of the mailbox thread. It proceeds in five numbered steps.\n\n### Step 0 \u2014 Out-of-Order and Pre-Abort Checks\n\n```java\nif (lastCheckpointId >= metadata.getCheckpointId()) {\n    channelStateWriter.abort(metadata.getCheckpointId(), new CancellationException(), true);\n    checkAndClearAbortedStatus(metadata.getCheckpointId());\n    return;\n}\nif (checkAndClearAbortedStatus(metadata.getCheckpointId())) {\n    operatorChain.broadcastEvent(new CancelCheckpointMarker(metadata.getCheckpointId()));\n    channelStateWriter.abort(...);\n    return;\n}\n```\n\n`abortedCheckpointIds` is a bounded `LinkedHashSet` (default size 50) that records checkpoints\naborted by the coordinator before the task's trigger RPC arrived. If the arriving checkpoint ID is\nalready in this set, a `CancelCheckpointMarker` is broadcast downstream immediately and no snapshot\nis taken.\n\n### Step 1 \u2014 Pre-Barrier Operator Work\n\n```java\noperatorChain.prepareSnapshotPreBarrier(metadata.getCheckpointId());\n```\n\nIterates operators in the chain (head to tail) and calls `prepareSnapshotPreBarrier`. Most\noperators do nothing here; it exists for operators that must flush or finalize output before the\nbarrier is emitted (e.g., operators that buffer records for sorting).\n\n### Step 2 \u2014 Barrier Broadcast\n\n```java\nCheckpointBarrier checkpointBarrier =\n    new CheckpointBarrier(metadata.getCheckpointId(), metadata.getTimestamp(), options);\noperatorChain.broadcastEvent(checkpointBarrier, options.isUnalignedCheckpoint());\n```\n\n`broadcastEvent` serializes the `CheckpointBarrier` into a network buffer and writes it to every\noutput subpartition. For unaligned checkpoints, the barrier is written as a **priority event**,\nwhich causes the network layer to move it ahead of any already-queued data buffers in the\nsubpartition. The in-flight output data that was ahead of the barrier is captured by the\n`ChannelStateWriter` during this broadcast.\n\n### Step 3 \u2014 Alignment Timeout Registration\n\n```java\nregisterAlignmentTimer(metadata.getCheckpointId(), operatorChain, checkpointBarrier);\n```\n\nOnly active when `checkpointOptions.isTimeoutable()` (i.e., `alignedCheckpointTimeout > 0`). A\ntimer is scheduled for `timerDelay = max(0, alignedCheckpointTimeout - elapsed)` milliseconds. On\nexpiry, `operatorChain.alignedBarrierTimeout(checkpointId)` is called, which propagates to\n`SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler.alignedBarrierTimeout()`, triggering the aligned\u2192unaligned\nconversion in the barrier handler state machine.\n\n### Step 4 \u2014 Channel State Output Finalization\n\n```java\nif (options.needsChannelState()) {\n    channelStateWriter.finishOutput(metadata.getCheckpointId());\n}\n```\n\nSignals to the `ChannelStateWriter` that all output buffers for this checkpoint have been written.\nThe writer can now finalize the output channel state futures.\n\n### Step 5 \u2014 Synchronous Snapshot and Async Handoff\n\n```java\nif (takeSnapshotSync(snapshotFutures, metadata, metrics, options, operatorChain, isRunning)) {\n    finishAndReportAsync(snapshotFutures, metadata, metrics, ...);\n}\n```\n\n**`takeSnapshotSync`**:\n1. Retrieves `ChannelStateWriteResult` from the writer (contains futures for input/output channel\n   state handles).\n2. Resolves `CheckpointStreamFactory` from `checkpointStorage` (cached per checkpoint ID).\n3. Calls `operatorChain.snapshotState(...)`, which iterates operators tail-to-head and calls\n   `operator.snapshotState(...)` on each. Each operator returns an `OperatorSnapshotFutures`\n   containing futures for managed state, raw state, and channel state.\n4. Records `syncDurationMillis`.\n\n**`finishAndReportAsync`**:\n1. Constructs `AsyncCheckpointRunnable` with the map of `OperatorSnapshotFutures`.\n2. Registers it in `checkpoints: Map<Long, AsyncCheckpointRunnable>`.\n3. Submits to `asyncOperationsThreadPool`.\n\nThe mailbox thread is released immediately after step 5; all state materialization happens\nasynchronously.\n\n### AsyncCheckpointRunnable Execution\n\n```\nAsyncCheckpointRunnable.run()\n  \u2514\u2500 finalizeNonFinishedSnapshots()\n       \u2514\u2500 for each operator: OperatorSnapshotFinalizer.create(snapshotInProgress)\n            \u2514\u2500 materializes managed/raw state futures, collects handles\n  \u2514\u2500 reportCompletedSnapshotStates(jobManagerTaskOperatorSubtaskStates, ...)\n       \u2514\u2500 taskEnvironment.getTaskStateManager().reportTaskStateSnapshots(...)\n            \u2514\u2500 localStateStore.storeLocalState(checkpointId, localState)\n            \u2514\u2500 checkpointResponder.acknowledgeCheckpoint(jobId, executionAttemptID, checkpointId,\n                                                         checkpointMetrics, acknowledgedState)\n```\n\n`RpcCheckpointResponder.acknowledgeCheckpoint()` serializes the `TaskStateSnapshot` and sends it\nvia `checkpointCoordinatorGateway.acknowledgeCheckpoint()` \u2014 an RPC back to the JobManager's\n`CheckpointCoordinatorGateway`.\n\n---\n\n## 4. Barrier Reception \u2014 Downstream Tasks\n\n### 4.1 CheckpointedInputGate \u2014 Network Event Dispatch\n\n`CheckpointedInputGate` wraps the `InputGate` and intercepts all checkpoint-related network events\nin `pollNext()`:\n\n```java\n// CheckpointedInputGate.handleEvent()\nif (eventClass == CheckpointBarrier.class) {\n    barrierHandler.processBarrier(checkpointBarrier, channelInfo, false);\n} else if (eventClass == CancelCheckpointMarker.class) {\n    barrierHandler.processCancellationBarrier(cancelMarker, channelInfo);\n} else if (eventClass == EventAnnouncement.class) {\n    // unaligned: barrier announcement arrives before the barrier itself\n    barrierHandler.processBarrierAnnouncement(announcedBarrier, sequenceNumber, channelInfo);\n} else if (eventClass == EndOfPartitionEvent.class) {\n    barrierHandler.processEndOfPartition(channelInfo);\n}\n```\n\nFor unaligned checkpoints, the network layer sends an `EventAnnouncement` as a priority event\nbefore the actual `CheckpointBarrier`. `CheckpointedInputGate` registers a callback on\n`inputGate.getPriorityEventAvailableFuture()` that posts a `MailOptions.urgent()` mail to process\npriority events immediately, ahead of normal record processing.\n\n### 4.2 Handler Selection\n\nTwo `CheckpointBarrierHandler` implementations exist:\n\n| Handler                        | Guarantee     | Mechanism                                      |\n|--------------------------------|---------------|------------------------------------------------|\n| `SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler` | Exactly-once | Blocks channels; state machine per checkpoint  |\n| `CheckpointBarrierTracker`     | At-least-once | Counts barriers; no blocking                   |\n\nThe handler is selected at `CheckpointedInputGate` construction time based on\n`isExactlyOnceMode`.\n\n---\n\n## 5. Aligned Barrier Handling \u2014 SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler\n\n### 5.1 checkNewCheckpoint \u2014 First Barrier Arrival\n\n```java\n// SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler.processBarrier()\nif (barrier.getId() > currentCheckpointId) {\n    if (isCheckpointPending()) {\n        cancelSubsumedCheckpoint(barrier.getId());  // abort older checkpoint\n    }\n    currentCheckpointId = barrier.getId();\n    pendingCheckpointBarrier = barrier;\n    alignedChannels.clear();\n    targetChannelCount = numOpenChannels;\n    allBarriersReceivedFuture = new CompletableFuture<>();\n    registerAlignmentTimer(barrier);\n}\n```\n\nOn the first barrier for a new checkpoint ID, the handler resets alignment state and optionally\nregisters a timeout timer. If a prior checkpoint was still pending, it is subsumed\n(`CHECKPOINT_DECLINED_SUBSUMED`).\n\n### 5.2 BarrierHandlerState State Machine\n\nThe handler delegates all state transitions to a `BarrierHandlerState` implementation. The state\nmachine has six concrete states:\n\n```\nAligned (non-timeoutable):\n  WaitingForFirstBarrier\n    \u2500\u2500[barrierReceived]\u2500\u2500\u25ba CollectingBarriers\n    \u2500\u2500[allBarriersReceived in CollectingBarriers]\u2500\u2500\u25ba triggerGlobalCheckpoint \u2500\u2500\u25ba WaitingForFirstBarrier\n\nAlternating (timeoutable, aligned start):\n  AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier\n    \u2500\u2500[barrierReceived]\u2500\u2500\u25ba AlternatingCollectingBarriers\n    \u2500\u2500[alignedCheckpointTimeout]\u2500\u2500\u25ba AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned\n    \u2500\u2500[allBarriersReceived in AlternatingCollectingBarriers]\u2500\u2500\u25ba trigger \u2500\u2500\u25ba AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier\n\nAlternating (timeoutable, unaligned start or post-timeout):\n  AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned\n    \u2500\u2500[barrierReceived]\u2500\u2500\u25ba initInputsCheckpoint + triggerGlobalCheckpoint \u2500\u2500\u25ba AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned\n    \u2500\u2500[allBarriersReceived in AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned]\u2500\u2500\u25ba AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier\n```\n\n**`AbstractAlignedBarrierHandlerState.barrierReceived`** (aligned path):\n\n```java\nif (markChannelBlocked) {\n    state.blockChannel(channelInfo);   // suspends reads from this channel\n}\nif (controller.allBarriersReceived()) {\n    controller.triggerGlobalCheckpoint(checkpointBarrier);\n    state.unblockAllChannels();\n    return new WaitingForFirstBarrier(state.getInputs());\n}\nreturn convertAfterBarrierReceived(state);  // WaitingForFirstBarrier\u2192CollectingBarriers\n```\n\n`controller.allBarriersReceived()` checks `alignedChannels.size() == targetChannelCount`. Channel\nblocking is implemented by suspending credit grants to the upstream channel, applying backpressure\nwithout dropping data.\n\n**`AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned.barrierReceived`** (unaligned path):\n\n```java\nCheckpointBarrier unalignedBarrier = checkpointBarrier.asUnaligned();\ncontroller.initInputsCheckpoint(unalignedBarrier);   // starts ChannelStateWriter\nfor (CheckpointableInput input : channelState.getInputs()) {\n    input.checkpointStarted(unalignedBarrier);        // captures in-flight input buffers\n}\ncontroller.triggerGlobalCheckpoint(unalignedBarrier); // triggers immediately on first barrier\n```\n\nThe checkpoint is triggered on the **first** barrier received, regardless of how many channels\nremain. In-flight input buffers (data that arrived after the barrier was sent but before it was\nreceived) are captured by `ChannelStateWriter` and stored as part of the checkpoint. This\neliminates alignment stalls at the cost of larger checkpoint state.\n\n### 5.3 Aligned\u2192Unaligned Timeout Conversion\n\nWhen `alignedCheckpointTimeout` elapses during alignment:\n\n```\nSingleCheckpointBarrierHandler.alignedBarrierTimeout(checkpointId)\n  \u2514\u2500 currentState = currentState.alignedCheckpointTimeout(controller, pendingCheckpointBarrier)\n```\n\nIn `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier.alignedCheckpointTimeout`:\n\n```java\nstate.prioritizeAllAnnouncements();  // promote queued announcements to priority events\nreturn new AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned(true, state);\n```\n\nIn `AlternatingCollectingBarriers.alignedCheckpointTimeout` (barriers already partially received):\n\n```java\n// triggers checkpoint immediately, unblocks channels, captures remaining in-flight data\ncontroller.initInputsCheckpoint(checkpointBarrier.asUnaligned());\nfor (CheckpointableInput input : channelState.getInputs()) {\n    input.checkpointStarted(checkpointBarrier.asUnaligned());\n}\ncontroller.triggerGlobalCheckpoint(checkpointBarrier.asUnaligned());\nreturn new AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned(true, channelState);\n```\n\nThe already-blocked channels are unblocked; their in-flight data is captured by the channel state\nwriter. The checkpoint completes without waiting for remaining barriers.\n\n### 5.4 triggerCheckpoint \u2192 performCheckpoint\n\n`controller.triggerGlobalCheckpoint(barrier)` calls\n`SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler.triggerCheckpoint(barrier)`, which calls\n`toNotifyOnCheckpoint.triggerCheckpointOnBarrier(checkpointMetaData, checkpointOptions, metrics)`.\nThis re-enters `StreamTask.performCheckpoint()`, which calls\n`subtaskCheckpointCoordinator.checkpointState()` \u2014 the same five-step process described in\nSection 3, but now for a downstream (non-source) task.\n\n---\n\n## 6. At-Least-Once Barrier Handling \u2014 CheckpointBarrierTracker\n\n`CheckpointBarrierTracker` provides at-least-once semantics by counting barriers without blocking\nchannels. Records from channels that have already sent a barrier continue to be processed while\nwaiting for remaining barriers.\n\n### 6.1 Data Structures\n\n```java\nprivate final ArrayDeque<CheckpointBarrierCount> pendingCheckpoints;  // max 50 entries\nprivate long latestPendingCheckpointID = -1;\n```\n\n`CheckpointBarrierCount` tracks per-checkpoint state:\n- `checkpointId`\n- `targetChannelCount` (= `numOpenChannels` at first barrier)\n- `alignedChannels: Set<InputChannelInfo>` (channels that sent a barrier)\n- `aborted: boolean`\n\n### 6.2 processBarrier Logic\n\n```java\n// Fast path: single channel\nif (barrierId > latestPendingCheckpointID && numOpenChannels == 1) {\n    notifyCheckpoint(receivedBarrier);\n    return;\n}\n\n// General path\nCheckpointBarrierCount barrierCount = findInQueue(barrierId);\nif (barrierCount != null) {\n    int count = barrierCount.markChannelAligned(channelInfo);\n    if (count == barrierCount.getTargetChannelCount()) {\n        // remove this and all prior pending checkpoints (subsumed)\n        for (int i = 0; i <= pos; i++) pendingCheckpoints.pollFirst();\n        if (!barrierCount.isAborted()) triggerCheckpointOnAligned(barrierCount);\n    }\n} else if (barrierId > latestPendingCheckpointID) {\n    latestPendingCheckpointID = barrierId;\n    pendingCheckpoints.addLast(new CheckpointBarrierCount(receivedBarrier, channelInfo, numOpenChannels));\n    if (pendingCheckpoints.size() > MAX_CHECKPOINTS_TO_TRACK) pendingCheckpoints.pollFirst();\n}\n```\n\nMultiple checkpoints can be simultaneously pending in the deque. When a checkpoint completes, all\nprior entries are removed (subsumed). The tracker supports up to 50 concurrent pending checkpoints;\nolder ones are evicted if the limit is exceeded.\n\n### 6.3 CancelCheckpointMarker Handling\n\n```java\n// processCancellationBarrier()\nwhile ((cbc = pendingCheckpoints.peekFirst()) != null && cbc.checkpointId() < checkpointId) {\n    pendingCheckpoints.removeFirst();\n    if (cbc.markAborted()) notifyAbortOnCancellationBarrier(cbc.checkpointId());\n}\nif (cbc != null && cbc.checkpointId() == checkpointId) {\n    if (cbc.markAborted()) notifyAbortOnCancellationBarrier(checkpointId);\n    if (cbc.markChannelAligned(channelInfo) == cbc.getTargetChannelCount()) {\n        pendingCheckpoints.removeFirst();  // all channels seen, clean up\n    }\n}\n```\n\nCancellation barriers abort all pending checkpoints with IDs less than the cancelled ID, then mark\nthe target checkpoint as aborted. The entry is retained until all channels have sent their\ncancellation barrier, at which point it is removed.\n\n---\n\n## 7. PendingCheckpoint Lifecycle\n\n`PendingCheckpoint` is annotated `@NotThreadSafe`; all access is serialized under the coordinator's\n`lock` object.\n\n### 7.1 Construction State\n\n```java\n// Key fields at construction\nMap<ExecutionAttemptID, ExecutionVertex> notYetAcknowledgedTasks;   // tasks still to ack\nSet<ExecutionAttemptID> acknowledgedTasks;                           // tasks that have acked\nMap<OperatorID, OperatorState> operatorStates;                       // accumulated state handles\nSet<OperatorID> notYetAcknowledgedOperatorCoordinators;\nSet<String> notYetAcknowledgedMasterStates;\nCompletableFuture<CompletedCheckpoint> onCompletionPromise;\nScheduledFuture<?> cancellerHandle;                                  // timeout canceller\n```\n\n### 7.2 acknowledgeTask\n\n```java\npublic TaskAcknowledgeResult acknowledgeTask(\n        ExecutionAttemptID executionAttemptId,\n        TaskStateSnapshot operatorSubtaskStates,\n        CheckpointMetrics metrics) {\n    synchronized (lock) {\n        if (disposed) return DISCARDED;\n        ExecutionVertex vertex = notYetAcknowledgedTasks.remove(executionAttemptId);\n        if (vertex == null) {\n            return acknowledgedTasks.contains(executionAttemptId) ? DUPLICATE : UNKNOWN;\n        }\n        acknowledgedTasks.add(executionAttemptId);\n        // merge operator subtask states into operatorStates map\n        for (OperatorIDPair pair : vertex.getJobVertex().getOperatorIDs()) {\n            updateOperatorState(vertex, operatorSubtaskStates, pair);\n        }\n        ++numAcknowledgedTasks;\n        // update stats (alignment duration, bytes persisted, etc.)\n        return SUCCESS;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n`updateOperatorState` creates or updates an `OperatorState` entry in `operatorStates`, keyed by\n`OperatorID`. Each `OperatorState` accumulates `OperatorSubtaskState` entries indexed by subtask\nindex, building the complete per-operator state picture across all parallelism instances.\n\n### 7.3 isFullyAcknowledged\n\n```java\npublic boolean isFullyAcknowledged() {\n    return areTasksFullyAcknowledged()          // notYetAcknowledgedTasks.isEmpty()\n        && areCoordinatorsFullyAcknowledged()   // notYetAcknowledgedOperatorCoordinators.isEmpty()\n        && areMasterStatesFullyAcknowledged();  // notYetAcknowledgedMasterStates.isEmpty()\n}\n```\n\nAll three sets must be empty. Coordinator acknowledgments arrive via\n`acknowledgeCoordinatorState()` (called by `OperatorCoordinatorCheckpoints`); master state\nacknowledgments arrive via `acknowledgeMasterState()` (called by `MasterHooks`).\n\n### 7.4 finalizeCheckpoint \u2014 PendingCheckpoint \u2192 CompletedCheckpoint\n\n```java\npublic CompletedCheckpoint finalizeCheckpoint(\n        CheckpointsCleaner checkpointsCleaner, Runnable postCleanup, Executor executor)\n        throws IOException {\n    synchronized (lock) {\n        checkState(!isDisposed());\n        checkState(isFullyAcknowledged());\n\n        checkpointPlan.fulfillFinishedTaskStatus(operatorStates);\n\n        // Serialize checkpoint metadata to storage\n        CheckpointMetadata savepoint =\n            new CheckpointMetadata(checkpointId, operatorStates.values(), masterStates, props);\n        CompletedCheckpointStorageLocation finalizedLocation;\n        try (CheckpointMetadataOutputStream out = targetLocation.createMetadataOutputStream()) {\n            Checkpoints.storeCheckpointMetadata(savepoint, out);\n            finalizedLocation = out.closeAndFinalizeCheckpoint();\n        }\n\n        CompletedCheckpoint completed = new CompletedCheckpoint(\n            jobId, checkpointId, checkpointTimestamp, System.currentTimeMillis(),\n            operatorStates, masterStates, props, finalizedLocation, stats);\n\n        dispose(false, checkpointsCleaner, postCleanup, executor);  // mark disposed, keep state\n        return completed;\n    }\n}\n```\n\n`Checkpoints.storeCheckpointMetadata` serializes the `CheckpointMetadata` (operator states,\nmaster states, properties) to the `CheckpointMetadataOutputStream`. The stream is backed by the\nconfigured `CheckpointStorage` (filesystem, S3, etc.). `closeAndFinalizeCheckpoint()` atomically\ncommits the metadata file and returns a `CompletedCheckpointStorageLocation` containing the\n`externalPointer` (e.g., `hdfs:///checkpoints/job-id/chk-42/_metadata`).\n\n### 7.5 abort\n\n```java\npublic void abort(CheckpointFailureReason reason, Throwable cause,\n                  CheckpointsCleaner cleaner, Runnable postCleanup,\n                  Executor executor, CheckpointStatsTracker statsTracker) {\n    failureCause = new CheckpointException(reason, cause);\n    onCompletionPromise.completeExceptionally(failureCause);\n    masterTriggerCompletionPromise.completeExceptionally(failureCause);\n    dispose(true, cleaner, postCleanup, executor);  // releaseState=true: discard state handles\n}\n```\n\n`dispose(releaseState=true)` calls `checkpointsCleaner.cleanCheckpoint(this, true, ...)`, which\nasynchronously discards all accumulated state handles to prevent storage leaks.\n\n---\n\n## 8. Checkpoint Completion \u2014 Coordinator Side\n\n### 8.1 receiveAcknowledgeMessage\n\n```java\n// CheckpointCoordinator.receiveAcknowledgeMessage()\nsynchronized (lock) {\n    // Register shared state regardless of checkpoint status (prevents premature GC)\n    if (message.getSubtaskState() != null && !checkpoint.getProps().isSavepoint()) {\n        message.getSubtaskState().registerSharedStates(\n            completedCheckpointStore.getSharedStateRegistry(), checkpointId);\n    }\n\n    switch (checkpoint.acknowledgeTask(executionAttemptId, subtaskState, metrics)) {\n        case SUCCESS:\n            if (checkpoint.isFullyAcknowledged()) {\n                completePendingCheckpoint(checkpoint);\n            }\n            break;\n        case DUPLICATE: /* log and ignore */\n        case UNKNOWN:   /* discard state handles */\n        case DISCARDED: /* discard state handles */\n    }\n}\n```\n\nShared state (incremental RocksDB SST files) is registered in the `SharedStateRegistry` before\nthe acknowledgment is processed. This prevents the registry from garbage-collecting state that\nmight be referenced by a late-arriving acknowledgment.\n\n### 8.2 completePendingCheckpoint\n\n```java\nprivate void completePendingCheckpoint(PendingCheckpoint pendingCheckpoint)\n        throws CheckpointException {\n    final long checkpointId = pendingCheckpoint.getCheckpointID();\n\n    // (1) Mark shared state as checkpoint-complete in registry\n    completedCheckpointStore.getSharedStateRegistry().checkpointCompleted(checkpointId);\n\n    // (2) Finalize: write metadata, create CompletedCheckpoint\n    CompletedCheckpoint completedCheckpoint = finalizeCheckpoint(pendingCheckpoint);\n\n    // (3) Persist to HA store, subsume oldest checkpoint\n    CompletedCheckpoint lastSubsumed = null;\n    if (!props.isSavepoint()) {\n        lastSubsumed = addCompletedCheckpointToStoreAndSubsumeOldest(\n            checkpointId, completedCheckpoint, pendingCheckpoint);\n    }\n\n    // (4) Report stats, complete the caller's future\n    reportCompletedCheckpoint(completedCheckpoint);\n    pendingCheckpoint.getCompletionFuture().complete(completedCheckpoint);\n\n    // (5) Remove from pending map, schedule next trigger\n    pendingCheckpoints.remove(checkpointId);\n    scheduleTriggerRequest();\n\n    // (6) Cleanup: drop subsumed pending checkpoints, notify tasks\n    cleanupAfterCompletedCheckpoint(pendingCheckpoint, checkpointId,\n                                    completedCheckpoint, lastSubsumed, props);\n}\n```\n\n**`addCompletedCheckpointToStoreAndSubsumeOldest`** calls\n`completedCheckpointStore.addCheckpointAndSubsumeOldestOne(...)`. The store (ZooKeeper-backed in\nHA mode, in-memory otherwise) retains at most `maxNumberOfCheckpointsToRetain` entries. The\nevicted checkpoint's state handles are asynchronously discarded via `CheckpointsCleaner`.\n\n### 8.3 sendAcknowledgeMessages \u2014 Notifying Tasks\n\n```java\nvoid sendAcknowledgeMessages(List<ExecutionVertex> tasksToCommit,\n                              long completedCheckpointId, long completedTimestamp,\n                              long lastSubsumedCheckpointId) {\n    // Notify tasks (RPC to TaskExecutors)\n    for (ExecutionVertex ev : tasksToCommit) {\n        Execution ee = ev.getCurrentExecutionAttempt();\n        if (ee != null) {\n            ee.notifyCheckpointOnComplete(completedCheckpointId, completedTimestamp,\n                                          lastSubsumedCheckpointId);\n        }\n    }\n    // Notify operator coordinators (in-process)\n    for (OperatorCoordinatorCheckpointContext ctx : coordinatorsToCheckpoint) {\n        ctx.notifyCheckpointComplete(completedCheckpointId);\n    }\n}\n```\n\n`notifyCheckpointOnComplete` sends an RPC to each `TaskExecutor`, which calls\n`task.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)` \u2192 `StreamTask.notifyCheckpointCompleteAsync()` \u2192\nmailbox \u2192 `subtaskCheckpointCoordinator.notifyCheckpointComplete()` \u2192 iterates operators and calls\n`operator.notifyCheckpointComplete(checkpointId)`. This is where operators commit external\nside-effects (e.g., Kafka offset commits, two-phase commit sinks).\n\n---\n\n## 9. Abort and Decline Paths\n\n### 9.1 Task Decline\n\nA task declines a checkpoint by calling `checkpointResponder.declineCheckpoint()`, which sends a\n`DeclineCheckpoint` RPC to the coordinator. `receiveDeclineMessage()` calls\n`abortPendingCheckpoint(checkpoint, exception, executionAttemptID)`.\n\n### 9.2 abortPendingCheckpoint\n\n```java\nprivate void abortPendingCheckpoint(PendingCheckpoint pendingCheckpoint,\n                                     CheckpointException exception,\n                                     ExecutionAttemptID executionAttemptID) {\n    assert Thread.holdsLock(lock);\n    if (!pendingCheckpoint.isDisposed()) {\n        try {\n            pendingCheckpoint.abort(reason, cause, checkpointsCleaner,\n                                    this::scheduleTriggerRequest, executor, statsTracker);\n            failureManager.handleCheckpointException(...);\n        } finally {\n            sendAbortedMessages(tasksToCommitTo, checkpointId, timestamp);\n            pendingCheckpoints.remove(checkpointId);\n            if (reason == CHECKPOINT_EXPIRED) rememberRecentExpiredCheckpointId(checkpointId);\n            scheduleTriggerRequest();\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\n`sendAbortedMessages` dispatches `notifyCheckpointAborted` RPCs to all tasks asynchronously (via\n`executor.execute(...)` to avoid blocking the coordinator lock). Tasks receiving this notification\ncall `StreamTask.notifyCheckpointAbortAsync()` \u2192 operators' `notifyCheckpointAborted()`.\n\n### 9.3 CheckpointCanceller \u2014 Timeout\n\n```java\nclass CheckpointCanceller implements Runnable {\n    public void run() {\n        synchronized (lock) {\n            if (!pendingCheckpoint.isDisposed()) {\n                abortPendingCheckpoint(pendingCheckpoint,\n                    new CheckpointException(CheckpointFailureReason.CHECKPOINT_EXPIRED));\n            }\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nRegistered at `PendingCheckpoint` creation via `timer.schedule(checkpointTimeout, MILLISECONDS)`.\nThe canceller handle is stored in `PendingCheckpoint.cancellerHandle` and cancelled when the\ncheckpoint completes or is aborted.\n\n### 9.4 CancelCheckpointMarker Propagation\n\nWhen a checkpoint is aborted at the coordinator, `sendAbortedMessages` notifies tasks. Tasks that\nhave already emitted a barrier for the aborted checkpoint broadcast a `CancelCheckpointMarker`\ndownstream via `operatorChain.broadcastEvent(new CancelCheckpointMarker(checkpointId))`. Downstream\ntasks receiving this marker call `barrierHandler.processCancellationBarrier()`, which aborts the\npending checkpoint in the barrier handler and notifies the task.\n\n### 9.5 dropSubsumedCheckpoints\n\n```java\nprivate void dropSubsumedCheckpoints(long checkpointId) {\n    abortPendingCheckpoints(\n        checkpoint -> checkpoint.getCheckpointID() < checkpointId && checkpoint.canBeSubsumed(),\n        new CheckpointException(CheckpointFailureReason.CHECKPOINT_SUBSUMED));\n}\n```\n\nCalled after a checkpoint completes. Any pending checkpoint with a lower ID that is not a savepoint\n(`canBeSubsumed()` returns `false` for savepoints) is aborted. This handles the case where a newer\ncheckpoint completes before an older one.\n\n---\n\n## 10. CompletedCheckpoint Structure\n\n```java\npublic class CompletedCheckpoint implements Serializable, Checkpoint {\n    private final JobID job;\n    private final long checkpointID;\n    private final long timestamp;               // trigger time\n    private final long completionTimestamp;     // finalization time\n    private final Map<OperatorID, OperatorState> operatorStates;\n    private final Collection<MasterState> masterHookStates;\n    private final CheckpointProperties props;\n    private final CompletedCheckpointStorageLocation storageLocation;\n    private final StreamStateHandle metadataHandle;  // handle to _metadata file\n    private final String externalPointer;            // e.g., \"hdfs:///chk-42\"\n}\n```\n\n`OperatorState` contains:\n- `Map<Integer, OperatorSubtaskState>` \u2014 subtask index \u2192 state handles\n- `StreamStateHandle coordinatorState` \u2014 operator coordinator state\n- Parallelism metadata for rescaling validation\n\n`OperatorSubtaskState` contains handles for:\n- Managed keyed state (RocksDB SST files or heap snapshots)\n- Raw keyed state\n- Managed operator state\n- Raw operator state\n- Input channel state (unaligned checkpoints)\n- Result subpartition state (unaligned checkpoints)\n\n---\n\n## 11. Key Design Properties\n\n### 11.1 Exactly-Once vs. At-Least-Once\n\n| Property                  | Exactly-Once (`SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler`) | At-Least-Once (`CheckpointBarrierTracker`) |\n|---------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|---------------------------------------------|\n| Channel blocking          | Yes \u2014 backpressure after first barrier           | No \u2014 all channels remain open               |\n| Trigger condition         | All barriers received                            | All barriers received (counted only)        |\n| In-flight data at trigger | None (aligned) or captured (unaligned)           | May include post-barrier records            |\n| Concurrent checkpoints    | One per handler                                  | Up to 50 tracked simultaneously             |\n| Overhead                  | Alignment stall or channel state overhead        | Minimal                                     |\n\n### 11.2 Aligned vs. Unaligned Checkpoints\n\n| Property                  | Aligned                                    | Unaligned                                        |\n|---------------------------|--------------------------------------------|--------------------------------------------------|\n| Barrier position          | In-order with data                         | Jumps ahead of buffered data                     |\n| Trigger timing            | After all barriers received                | On first barrier received                        |\n| Channel state             | Not captured                               | Input and output in-flight buffers captured      |\n| Checkpoint size           | Operator state only                        | Operator state + channel state                   |\n| Alignment stall           | Yes, proportional to skew                  | None                                             |\n| Recovery complexity       | Replay from checkpoint                     | Replay channel state + operator state            |\n| Network priority          | Normal event                               | Priority event (overtakes data buffers)          |\n| Mailbox priority          | Normal                                     | `MailOptions.urgent()`                           |\n\n### 11.3 Alternating Checkpoints\n\nThe alternating mode (`alignedCheckpointTimeout > 0`) starts each checkpoint as aligned and\nconverts to unaligned if alignment takes longer than the configured timeout. This provides:\n\n- Low overhead (no channel state) when the pipeline is healthy and barriers arrive quickly.\n- Bounded checkpoint latency under backpressure by falling back to unaligned semantics.\n\nThe state machine transition `AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrier \u2192 AlternatingWaitingForFirstBarrierUnaligned`\n(on timeout before any barrier) and `AlternatingCollectingBarriers \u2192 AlternatingCollectingBarriersUnaligned`\n(on timeout after partial alignment) both call `state.prioritizeAllAnnouncements()` to promote\nqueued barrier announcements to priority events, ensuring the unaligned barriers are processed\nimmediately.\n\n### 11.4 Concurrency Model\n\n| Component                        | Thread                          | Synchronization                    |\n|----------------------------------|---------------------------------|------------------------------------|\n| `CheckpointCoordinator`          | Timer thread (single-threaded)  | `synchronized (lock)` for state    |\n| `PendingCheckpoint`              | Timer thread                    | `synchronized (lock)` internally   |\n| `AsyncCheckpointRunnable`        | `asyncOperationsThreadPool`     | Atomic CAS on `asyncCheckpointState` |\n| `SubtaskCheckpointCoordinatorImpl` | Mailbox thread               | `synchronized (lock)` for `checkpoints` map |\n| `SingleCheckpointBarrierHandler` | Mailbox thread                  | Single-threaded (mailbox)          |\n| `ChannelStateWriter`             | Dedicated writer thread         | Internal queue                     |\n\nThe coordinator's `lock` object is held during all `pendingCheckpoints` map mutations and during\n`completePendingCheckpoint`. The `PendingCheckpoint.lock` is a separate object, allowing\n`acknowledgeTask` to be called without holding the coordinator lock (though in practice the\ncoordinator always holds its own lock when calling `acknowledgeTask`).\n\n---\n\n## 12.
